  Jack's time to finish two-thirds of the work = (2/3) / (1/12) = 8 hours
  Jack's work = (2/3) of the yacht
  Jill's rate of cleaning = 1/20 of the yacht per hour
  Jill's work = (1/3) of the yacht
  Jill's time to finish the remaining one-third of the work = (1/3) / (1/20) = 6.67 hours

Action: Answer("E")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is 'x' hours.
  Then, the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel back by car is also 'x' hours.
  Total time taken by Mr. Sam = 17 hours
  Time taken if he goes both ways by train = 2x hours
  Time lost = 4 hours
  Therefore, 2x + 4 = 17
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 6.5 hours
  Time taken by Mr. Sam to travel back by car = x = 6.5 hours
  Total time taken by Mr. Sam if he had traveled by car in both ways = 2x = 13 hours
Action: Answer("E")

Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the number of copper coins is x and the number of brass coins is y.
  The amount of money the diver gets for each copper coin is 20 cents.
  The amount of money the diver gets for each brass coin is 25 cents.
  The total amount of money the diver got after one dive is $3.40.
  The equation that represents the total amount of money the diver got is 0.20x + 0.25y = 3.40.
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought.
  
Calculation:
  We can solve this problem using trial and error.
  If we assume that the diver brought 1 copper coin, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 0.20)/0.25 - 1 = 12.
  However, 12 is not a minimum number of brass coins that she brought because she could have brought fewer brass coins and more copper coins to get the same amount of money.
  If we assume that the diver brought 2 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 0.40)/0.25 - 2 = 10.
  This is a possible solution, but we need to check if there is a solution with fewer copper coins.
  If we assume that the diver brought 3 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 0.60)/0.25 - 3 = 8.
  This is a possible solution, but we need to check if there is a solution with fewer copper coins.
  If we assume that the diver brought 4 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 0.80)/0.25 - 4 = 6.
  This is a possible solution, but we need to check if there is a solution with fewer copper coins.
  If we assume that the diver brought 5 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 1.00)/0.25 - 5 = 4.
  This is a possible solution, but we need to check if there is a solution with fewer copper coins.
  If we assume that the diver brought 6 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 1.20)/0.25 - 6 = 2.
  This is a possible solution, but we need to check if there is a solution with fewer copper coins.
  If we assume that the diver brought 7 copper coins, then the number of brass coins she brought is (3.40 - 1.40)/0.25 - 7 = 0.
  This is a possible solution, and it is the solution with the minimum number of copper coins.
  
Answer: Answer("7")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 72 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let the three digit number be represented by ABC, where A, B, and C are the digits in the hundreds, tens, and ones places, respectively. 

From the problem statement, we know that:
A + B + C = 17  (Equation 1)
A^2 + B^2 + C^2 = 109  (Equation 2)
100A + 10B + C - 495 = 100C + 10B + A  (Equation 3)

Simplifying Equation 3, we get:
100A - A + 100B - 10B + C - 10C = 495
99A + 90B - 9C = 495
11A + 10B - C = 55  (Equation 4)

We can use Equation 1 to substitute C in terms of A and B:
C = 17 - A - B

Substituting this into Equation 2, we get:
A^2 + B^2 + (17 - A - B)^2 = 109
2A^2 + 2B^2 - 34A - 34B + 178 = 0
A^2 + B^2 - 17A - 17B + 89 = 0  (Equation 5)

We can use Equation 1 to substitute B in terms of A:
B = 17 - A - C
B = 17 - A - (17 - A - B)
2B = 34 - 2A
B = 17 - A  (Equation 6)

Substituting Equation 6 into Equation 5, we get:
A^2 + (17 - A)^2 - 17A - 17(17 - A) + 89 = 0
2A^2 - 34A + 90 = 0
A^2 - 17A + 45 = 0
(A - 5)(A - 12) = 0

Therefore, A = 5 or A = 12. However, since the number is a three digit number, A cannot be 12. Therefore, A = 5.

Using Equation 1, we can find B and C:
B = 17 - A - C = 17 - 5 - B = 12 - B
C = 17 - A - B = 17 - 5 - (12 - B) = B

Therefore, the number is 512, and when we subtract 495 from it, we get 17, which is the reverse of 512. 

Action: Answer("A")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 73 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Fernando has 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week.
  Fernando always goes home for dinner on Friday nights.
  Fernando has to allocate his meals for the remaining 6 days of the week.
  The number of ways to choose k items from a set of n distinct items is given by the binomial coefficient C(n,k) = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
  
Analysis:
  Fernando has to allocate 2 dinners and 3 lunches for the remaining 6 days of the week.
  He has 5 days to allocate the 3 lunches, which can be done in C(5,3) ways.
  He has 4 days to allocate the 2 dinners, which can be done in C(4,2) ways.
  Therefore, the total number of options to allocate his meals is C(5,3) * C(4,2).

Action: Answer("B")

  He has 4 days to allocate the 2 dinners, which can be done in C(4,2) ways.
  Therefore, the total number of options to allocate his meals is C(5,3) * C(4,2).

Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 74 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: 
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: 
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3, where s is the length of one side of the cube.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)r^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, the diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is V_cube / V_sphere.

Solution:
  Let s be the length of one side of the cube, and let r be the radius of the inscribed sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube, so 2r = s.
  Solving for r, we get r = s/2.
  The volume of the cube is V_cube = s^3.
  The volume of the sphere is V_sphere = (4/3)r^3 = (4/3)(s/2)^3 = (1/6)s^3.
  The ratio of the volumes is V_cube / V_sphere = s^3 / [(1/6)s^3] = (6/).
  Therefore, the answer is 6:.
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 75 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  This is a combination problem where we need to find the number of ways to divide 10 lime soda bottles into two groups of 5 each.
  The formula for combination is nCr = n! / (r! * (n-r)!), where n is the total number of items, and r is the number of items to be selected.
  We can also use the formula nCr = nC(n-r), which is useful when r is close to n/2.

Action: Answer("C")  
We need to find the number of ways to select 5 lime soda bottles out of 10, which is the same as selecting the remaining 5 bottles. Therefore, the number of ways to create two groups of 5 is:
10C5 = 10C(10-5) = 252 / (5! * 5!) = 252 / 120 = 21 / 2 = 126. Therefore, the answer is C.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus only.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm only.
  - Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W + B = 250.
  - We also know that W = 2.5B.
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V + B = 0.5(250) = 125.
  - We want to find the number of files that were not infected by a worm, which is (V + W).
  
Solution:
  - We know that W = 2.5B, so B = W/2.5.
  - We know that V + B = 125, so V + W/2.5 = 125.
  - Multiplying both sides by 2.5, we get 2.5V + W = 312.5.
  - Adding the equation V + W + B = 250 to 2.5V + W = 312.5, we get 3.5V + 2W + B = 562.5.
  - Substituting B = W/2.5, we get 3.5V + 4.5W = 562.5.
  - We want to find V + W, which is the number of files that were not infected by a worm.
  - We can solve for V by subtracting 2.5 times the equation W = 2.5B from 3.5V + 4.5W = 562.5:
    3.5V + 4.5W - 2.5W = 562.5 - 2.5B
    3.5V + 2W = 562.5 - 2.5(W/2.5)
    3.5V + 2W = 562.5 - W
    3.5V = 562.5 - 3W
    V = (562.5 - 3W)/3.5
  - Substituting this expression for V into V + W, we get:
    (562.5 - 3W)/3.5 + W
    (562.5 + 0.5W)/3.5
  - We want this expression to be an integer, so we need 0.5W to be a multiple of 3.5.
  - The smallest positive integer value of W that satisfies this is W = 7.
  - Substituting W = 7 into (562.5 + 0.5W)/3.5, we get (562.5 + 3.5)/3.5 = 161/2.
  - Therefore, the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is V + W = (562.5 - 3W)/3.5 + W = (562.5 - 3(7))/3.5 + 7 = 150.
Action: Answer("D")

  - Multiplying both sides by 2.5, we get 2.5V + W = 312.5.
  - Adding the equation V + W + B = 250 to 2.5V + W = 312.5, we get 3.5V + 2W + B = 562.5.
  - Substituting B = W/2.5, we get 3.5V + 4.5W = 562.5.
  - We want to find V + W, which is the number of files that were not infected by a worm.
  - We can solve for V by subtracting 2.5 times the equation W = 2.5B from 3.5V + 4.5W = 562.5:
    3.5V + 4.5W - 2.5W = 562.5 - 2.5B
    3.5V + 2W = 562.5 - 2.5(W/2.5)
    3.5V + 2W = 562.5 - W
    3.5V = 562.5 - 3W
    V = (562.5 - 3W)/3.5
  - Substituting this expression for V into V + W, we get:
    (562.5 - 3W)/3.5 + W
    (562.5 + 0.5W)/3.5
  - We want this expression to be an integer, so we need 0.5W to be a multiple of 3.5.
  - The smallest positive integer value of W that satisfies this is W = 7.
  - Substituting W = 7 into (562.5 + 0.5W)/3.5, we get (562.5 + 3.5)/3.5 = 161/2.
  - Therefore, the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is V + W = (562.5 - 3W)/3.5 + W = (562.5 - 3(7))/3.5 + 7 = 150.
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Profit% = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100
  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  We can use these formulas to solve the problem.
  
Action: 
  Let's assume the cost price of the article is x.
  Profit% = 20%
  Selling Price = Rs.360
  We can use the formula Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit to find the cost price.
  Rs.360 = x + (20/100)*x
  Rs.360 = x + 0.2x
  Rs.360 = 1.2x
  x = Rs.360 / 1.2
  x = Rs.300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
  Action: Answer("B")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 78 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
  The hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel buys 1 newspaper for $1 on each of the other days of the week, so it buys 5(x) newspapers from Monday to Friday.
  The hotel pays $4 for each newspaper on Sunday, so it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday for a total cost of $8x.
  The hotel pays $1 for each newspaper from Monday to Friday, so it buys 5(x) newspapers from Monday to Friday for a total cost of $5x.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers, so the total cost of the newspapers is $8x + $5x = $13x.
Action: 
  We know that the total cost of the newspapers is $210, so we can set up the equation:
  $13x = $210
  Solving for x:
  x = $210 / $13
  x  16.15
  The hotel buys approximately 16 newspapers on Monday.
  Answer("None of the Above")

  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers, so the total cost of the newspapers is $8x + $5x = $13x.
Action: 
  We know that the total cost of the newspapers is $210, so we can set up the equation:
  $13x = $210
  Solving for x:
  x = $210 / $13
  x  16.15
  The hotel buys approximately 16 newspapers on Monday.

Topic: Math
Question: The length of the ribbon was originally 30 cm. It was reduced in the ratio 5 : 3. What is its length now?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 30
  C: 6
  D: 15
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The ratio of 5:3 means that the original length was divided into 5+3=8 equal parts, and the reduced length is 5 out of those 8 parts.
  To find the reduced length, we can multiply the original length by the ratio 5/8.
Action: Answer("18/8 or 9/4 or E")  
Calculations: 
  The reduced length is (5/8) * 30 = 18.75 cm.
  The closest answer choice is E: 12, but the actual answer is 9/4 or 18/8.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The distance between X and Y is the same for both Allen and Bob.
  - Let's call the distance between X and Y "d".
  - Let's call the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time "t".
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, they have covered a total distance of "d".
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the second time, they have covered a total distance of "2d".
  - We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to solve the problem.
  
Solution:
  - Let's call the distance that Allen travels from X to Y "a".
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, Allen has covered "a" and Bob has covered "d - a".
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to write two equations:
    a = 54t
    d - a = 78t
  - Solving for "a" and "t", we get:
    a = 27d/31
    t = d/31
  - When Allen and Bob meet for the second time, Allen has covered "2a" and Bob has covered "2d - 2a + 48".
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to write two equations:
    2a = 78t
    2d - 2a + 48 = 54t
  - Substituting "a" and "t" from the previous equations, we get:
    2d - 54d/31 + 48 = 54d/31
  - Solving for "d", we get:
    d = 126 km
Action: Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 81 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume the distance travelled by the jeep is "d".
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep during the forward journey is "s".
  During the return journey, the speed of the jeep is "s+12".
  We know that distance = speed x time.
  During the forward journey, the time taken is 6 hours.
  During the return journey, the time taken is 4 hours.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed.
  We can set up two equations using the above information and solve for "d".
  Equation 1: d = s x 6
  Equation 2: d = (s+12) x 4
  We can solve for "s" by equating the two equations and then substitute the value of "s" in any of the above equations to find "d".
Action: Answer("C")  
Solution:
  From Equation 1, we get s = d/6.
  Substituting s in Equation 2, we get d = 4(d/6 + 12).
  Solving for d, we get d = 126km.
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 126km.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth rate is exponential.
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means that the number of water lilies doubles 30 times (since 2^30 is approximately equal to 1 billion).
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the lake will be fully covered with water lilies when there are 2^30 * 64 water lilies on the lake.
Action: 
  The number of water lilies on the lake doubles every two days, which means that the number of water lilies after n days is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means that we need to solve the equation 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30 * 64.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get n/2 = 30.
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get n = 60.
  Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 60 days.
Answer: Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M travels from City A to City B and takes 4 hours.
  Train N travels from City B to City A and takes 3.5 hours.
  The trains cross each other when their total distance traveled is equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  We can use the formula: time = distance / speed
  
Action: 
  Let's first find the distance between City A and City B.
  Let's assume that the speed of both trains is constant.
  Let's denote the speed of Train M as v1 and the speed of Train N as v2.
  Let's denote the time when the trains cross each other as t.
  Distance traveled by Train M = v1 * 4
  Distance traveled by Train N = v2 * 3.5
  Total distance traveled by both trains = v1 * 4 + v2 * 3.5
  Distance between City A and City B = v1 * 4 + v2 * 3.5
  Since the distance traveled by both trains is equal to the distance between City A and City B, we can write:
  v1 * 4 + v2 * 3.5 = distance between City A and City B
  We don't know the exact value of the distance between City A and City B, but we don't need it to find the time when the trains cross each other.
  We can solve for t using the formula:
  t = (distance between City A and City B) / (v1 + v2)
  Therefore, we need to find the value of (v1 + v2).
  We can use the formula: speed = distance / time
  Speed of Train M = v1 = (distance between City A and City B) / 4
  Speed of Train N = v2 = (distance between City A and City B) / 3.5
  Therefore, (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (1/4 + 1/3.5)
  (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (7.5/35)
  (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (3/14)
  Now, we can substitute the value of (v1 + v2) in the formula for t:
  t = (distance between City A and City B) / (v1 + v2)
  t = (distance between City A and City B) / ((distance between City A and City B) * (3/14))
  t = 14/3
  t = 4 hr 40 min
  The trains cross each other 4 hours and 40 minutes after Train M leaves City A, which is at 9:40 am.
  Therefore, the answer is not one of the given choices.
Response 1:

  Speed of Train N = v2 = (distance between City A and City B) / 3.5
  Therefore, (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (1/4 + 1/3.5)
  (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (7.5/35)
  (v1 + v2) = (distance between City A and City B) * (3/14)
  Now, we can substitute the value of (v1 + v2) in the formula for t:
  t = (distance between City A and City B) / (v1 + v2)
  t = (distance between City A and City B) / ((distance between City A and City B) * (3/14))
  t = 14/3
  t = 4 hr 40 min
  The trains cross each other 4 hours and 40 minutes after Train M leaves City A, which is at 9:40 am.
  Therefore, the answer is not one of the given choices.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  Let's call the sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles "S" and the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  We know that (S/10) = 12.2 and ((S+x)/11) = 14.8 (since the average increased by 2.6 tons).
  We can use these two equations to solve for x.
  Simplifying the second equation, we get S + x = 162.8.
  We can substitute the first equation into the second equation to get 10(12.2) + x = 162.8.
  Solving for x, we get x = 44.6.
Action: Answer("E")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The initial mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay.
  We want to remove and replace some of the mixture with pure sand to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
  Let's assume that we need to remove and replace x kg of the mixture.
  After removing and replacing x kg of the mixture, the amount of sand in the mixture will be 0.5(10-x) kg and the amount of clay in the mixture will also be 0.5(10-x) kg.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x.

Calculation:
  Initially, the mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay, which means that it contains 0.3*10 = 3 kg of sand and 0.7*10 = 7 kg of clay.
  After removing and replacing x kg of the mixture, the amount of sand in the mixture will be 0.5(10-x) kg.
  The amount of clay in the mixture will also be 0.5(10-x) kg.
  We want the mixture to contain equal quantities of clay and sand, which means that the amount of sand in the mixture should be equal to the amount of clay in the mixture.
  Therefore, we can set up the following equation:
  0.3*10 - 0.3x + x = 0.5(10-x)
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 4

Final Answer:
  We need to remove and replace 4 kg of the mixture with pure sand.
  To check, after removing and replacing 4 kg of the mixture, the amount of sand in the mixture will be 0.5(10-4) = 3 kg and the amount of clay in the mixture will also be 0.5(10-4) = 3 kg. Therefore, the mixture will contain equal quantities of clay and sand. 
  Action: Answer("D")

  We want the mixture to contain equal quantities of clay and sand, which means that the amount of sand in the mixture should be equal to the amount of clay in the mixture.
  Therefore, we can set up the following equation:
  0.3*10 - 0.3x + x = 0.5(10-x)
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 4

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To find the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers, we need to multiply the number of choices for each position.
  There are 26 choices for each of the two letter positions, and 10 choices for each of the two number positions.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers is 26 x 26 x 10 x 10 = 67600.
  All letters need to be distinct, since we are choosing two letters from a set of 26 without replacement.

Question: If Jill needed to buy 10 bottles of soda for a party in which 8 people attended, how many bottles of soda will she need to buy for a party in which 12 people are attending?
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 12
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Jill needed 10 bottles of soda for a party in which 8 people attended.
  This means that each person drank 10/8 = 1.25 bottles of soda.
  If Jill is now having a party with 12 people, she will need to buy 12 * 1.25 = 15 bottles of soda.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre  broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is L and the width is W.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is 2(L+W).
  The cost of gardening 1-meter boundary around the rectangular plot is the cost of gardening the length and width of the rectangular plot plus the cost of gardening the four corners.
  The cost of gardening is given as 10 per square meter.
  The area of the rectangular plot is L*W.
  The area of the 1-meter boundary is (L+2)*(W+2) - L*W = 2L + 2W + 4.
  The cost of gardening the rectangular plot is 10*L*W.
  The cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary is 10*(2L + 2W + 4).
  We are given that the perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 meters, so 2(L+W) = 340, which simplifies to L+W = 170.
Action: Answer("C")  
To find the cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary, we need to find the values of L and W. We have one equation with two variables, so we cannot determine the values of L and W. However, we can use the fact that the area of the rectangular plot is fixed to find the cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary. The area of the rectangular plot is L*W, which is equal to (L-2)*(W-2) + (2L + 2W + 4). We know that L+W = 170, so we can substitute W = 170-L into the equation for the area to get A = L(170-L) = -L^2 + 170L. The cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary is 10*(2L + 2W + 4) = 10*(2L + 2(170-L) + 4) = 10*(340-2L+4) = 10*(344-2L). The cost of gardening the rectangular plot is 10*L*W = 10*L*(170-L) = -10L^2 + 1700L. Therefore, the total cost of gardening is -10L^2 + 1700L + 10*(344-2L) = -10L^2 + 1740L + 3440. To find the minimum value of this quadratic function, we can use the formula L = -b/(2a) = -1740/(2*(-10)) = 87. The cost of gardening is then -10*87^2 + 1740*87 + 3440 = 298960. Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.

The cost of gardening the 1-meter boundary is 10*(2L + 2W + 4) = 10*(2L + 2(170-L) + 4) = 10*(340-2L+4) = 10*(344-2L). The cost of gardening the rectangular plot is 10*L*W = 10*L*(170-L) = -10L^2 + 1700L. Therefore, the total cost of gardening is -10L^2 + 1700L + 10*(344-2L) = -10L^2 + 1740L + 3440. To find the minimum value of this quadratic function, we can use the formula L = -b/(2a) = -1740/(2*(-10)) = 87. The cost of gardening is then -10*87^2 + 1740*87 + 3440 = 298960. Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.

Question: The capacity of a tank of dimensions (8 m  6 m  2.5 m) is
Choices:
  A: 120 litres
  B: 1200 litres
  C: 12000 litres
  D: 120000 litres
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Capacity of a tank is calculated by multiplying its length, width, and height.
  The given dimensions are in meters, so we need to convert the answer to liters.
  1 cubic meter = 1000 liters.
Calculation:
  Capacity = 8 m  6 m  2.5 m = 120 cubic meters
  Capacity in liters = 120 cubic meters  1000 liters/cubic meter = 120000 liters
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  Cost Price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the Selling Price and the Cost Price.
  Selling Price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450, so the Cost Price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold 90 kg of oranges at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg, so the Selling Price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.

Calculation:
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
         = Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5
         = Rs. 2.50
  Percentage gain = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
                  = (Rs. 2.50/Rs. 5) * 100
                  = 50%

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

Choices:
  A: 25 days
  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days
Response 0:

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joes fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Let's start by assigning variables to the ages of Joe, his sister, and his father. Let J be Joe's age, S be his sister's age, and F be his father's age. 

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his sister will be twice as old as she is now. Let's call the number of years until Joe is as old as his father "x". Then we have:

J + x = F
S + x = 2S

Simplifying the second equation, we get:

x = S

Substituting this into the first equation, we get:

J + S + F = 100
J + x + F = 100
F = 100 - J - x

Substituting the expressions for F and x into the second sentence, we get:

100 - J - x = 2(S - x)
100 - J - x = 2S - 2x
J + S + x = 50

Substituting x = S into this equation, we get:

J + S + S = 50
J + 2S = 50

Now we have three equations:

J + S + F = 100
J + x = F
J + 2S = 50

We can solve for J in the third equation:

J = 50 - 2S

Substituting this into the second equation, we get:

50 - 2S + x = F

Substituting this into the first equation, we get:

(50 - 2S) + S + (50 - 2S + x) = 100
100 - S - x = 4S - 100
200 - S - x = 4S
200 - x = 5S
S = 40

Substituting S = 40 into the equation for J, we get:

J = 50 - 2(40) = -30

This doesn't make sense, so we made a mistake somewhere. Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  For each head, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  For each tail, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After 20 flips, neither of them won or lost any amount.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on heads x times.
  Therefore, it landed on tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20-x) times.
  The total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan is 2x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is 3(20-x) = 60-3x.
  Since they didn't win or lose any amount, the total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan should be equal to the total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher.
  Therefore, 2x = 60-3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

  Therefore, it landed on tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20-x) times.
  The total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan is 2x.
  The total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher is 3(20-x) = 60-3x.
  Since they didn't win or lose any amount, the total amount given by Christopher to Jonathan should be equal to the total amount given by Jonathan to Christopher.
  Therefore, 2x = 60-3x.
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
Action: Answer("E")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Distance = Speed x Time
  - Let's call the distance between A and B "d"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B "t1"
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A "t2"
  - We know that t2 = t1 - 3 (since he has 3 hours left in his trip when he is 70 miles away from B)
  - We also know that d = 70 + 90 = 160 (since he drives the same distance twice)
  - We can use the formula Distance = Speed x Time to create an equation for each leg of the trip:
    - d = 70t1 (from A to B)
    - d = 90t2 (from B to A)
    - Substituting t2 = t1 - 3, we get d = 90(t1 - 3)
    - Setting the two expressions for d equal to each other, we get 70t1 = 90(t1 - 3)
    - Solving for t1, we get t1 = 27
Action: Answer("E")

Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve this problem, we need to use algebraic equations.
  Let's assume the 5 digit number is "abcde".
  According to the problem, if we add a 1 after it, the new number becomes "abcde1" and it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it, which is "1abcde".
  We can write this as an equation: 3(1abcde) = abcde1
  Simplifying this equation, we get: 299997a + 29997b + 2997c + 297d + 30e = 10a + b + c + d + e + 3
  Rearranging the terms, we get: 299986a + 29996b + 2967c + 267d = 27e + 3
  Since the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, e must be either 0 or 3.
  If e = 0, then the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 27, but the right-hand side is not. Therefore, e must be 3.
  Substituting e = 3 into the equation, we get: 299986a + 29996b + 2967c + 267d = 84
  Since the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, d must be either 0 or 3 or 6 or 9.
  If d = 0, then the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 9, but the right-hand side is not. Therefore, d must be either 3 or 6 or 9.
  Substituting d = 3 into the equation, we get: 299986a + 29996b + 2967c = 57
  Since the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 3, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 3. Therefore, c must be either 0 or 3 or 6 or 9.
  If c = 0, then the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 9, but the right-hand side is not. Therefore, c must be either 3 or 6 or 9.
  Substituting c = 3 into the equation, we get: 299986a + 29996b = 6
  Since the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 2, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 2. Therefore, b must be even.
  If b = 2, then the left-hand side of the equation is not an integer. Therefore, b must be 4 or 6 or 8.
  Substituting b = 4 into the equation, we get: 299986a = 2
  This is not possible, since a must be an integer between 1 and 9.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization and each employee contributes 'x' amount of money. 

So, the total amount collected by 'n' employees is n*x. 

According to the question, 
n*x = 6,00,000  ----(1) 

If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution per employee would be (x+60). 

So, the new total amount collected by 'n' employees is n*(x+60). 

According to the question, 
n*(x+60) = 6,24,000  ----(2) 

We need to find the value of 'n'. 

Let's solve the above two equations to get the value of 'n'. 

n*x = 6,00,000  ----(1) 
n*(x+60) = 6,24,000  ----(2) 

By solving the above two equations, we get x = 6000 and n = 100. 

Therefore, there are 100 employees in that organization. 

Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Then, each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
The total number of recipients is 5+4+2 = 11.
Therefore, we have:
5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600
25x + 16x + 2x = 8600/11
43x = 780
x = 780/43

So, each daughter receives 4x = 4(780/43) = Rs 320.

Therefore, the answer is A: Rs 400. 

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the number be x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, so he found (7/18)x.
  The actual value of 7/8 of the number is (7/8)x.
  The difference between the student's answer and the actual answer is 770.
  We can set up the equation: (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770
  To solve for x, we need to simplify the equation and solve for x.
  A: 1584 is not a solution to the equation.
  B: 2520 is not a solution to the equation.
  C: 1728 is not a solution to the equation.
  D: 1656 is a solution to the equation.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  We need to find the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50.
  We can use the formula: distance = (amount paid - initial fee) / cost per quarter mile + 0.25
  We have $8.50, and the initial fee is $3.50, so we have $5 left to spend on distance.
  The cost per quarter mile is $0.10.
Action: 
  distance = (8.50 - 3.50) / 0.10 + 0.25 = 50
  We can travel a maximum of 50 quarter-miles, which is 12.5 miles.
  Answer: Answer("B") 12.75 miles.
